# BenchBench research notes

Last researched: 2026-05-15

## Core take

BenchBench is a good idea if it judges whether a model can produce a *valid, useful, hard benchmark package*, not merely whether it can invent tasks that current models fail.

The major lesson from existing evals is that a benchmark is not just a prompt set. The best ones combine:

- a clear construct claim: what capability is being measured
- defensible item sourcing: expert-written, real-world, live, adversarial, or executable
- reliable scoring: objective answers, test harnesses, calibrated judges, or human preference aggregation
- human baselines: who can solve it and at what rate
- contamination controls: hidden/private splits, live refresh, new items, or provenance checks
- statistical analysis: discriminability, ranking stability, confidence intervals, item-level data
- update process: versioning, review, retirement of bad items, and fresh hard items as models improve

For BenchBench, the "frontier model cannot beat it by 50%" rule should be framed against humans, not absolute failure:

> A generated benchmark is frontier-resistant if qualified humans reach a high minimum score, while the best frontier solver reaches less than 50% of human performance under a fixed budget.

That avoids rewarding impossible, ambiguous, or ungradeable tasks.

## Benchmarks and what they actually do

### Broad knowledge and exam-style benchmarks

| Benchmark | What it tests | How it is built | How it scores | BenchBench lesson |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| MMLU | Broad multitask academic/professional knowledge | Multiple-choice questions across many subjects | Accuracy | Breadth makes adoption easy, but static exam-style datasets saturate and invite contamination. |
| MMLU-Pro | Harder multitask understanding and reasoning | Removes trivial/noisy MMLU items, adds harder reasoning questions, expands answer options from 4 to 10 | Accuracy, with prompt-stability analysis | A "better benchmark" can be a cleaned, harder, more stable version of a saturated one. BenchBench should reward item cleanup and prompt robustness, not just novelty. |
| GPQA | Graduate-level science Q&A | 448 multiple-choice questions written by biology, physics, and chemistry experts; designed to be hard even with web access | Accuracy; compares experts, skilled non-experts, and models | Expert construction plus human baselines are central. "Google-proof" is a useful property for generated benchmarks too. |
| Humanity's Last Exam | Expert-level closed-ended academic questions | 2,500 expert-authored multimodal questions across 100+ subjects; unambiguous, verifiable answers; designed against quick retrieval | Accuracy/calibration on closed-ended questions | Pre-screen against current models and require known, verifiable answers. This is close to BenchBench's desired benchmark object. |
| FrontierMath | Advanced math reasoning | Hundreds of original math problems crafted and vetted by expert mathematicians; some hidden/private | Exact answer or proof-style verification depending on problem | Originality and expert vetting matter, but very hard expert items need independent QA because grading/math errors become fatal. |

Sources: [MMLU](https://arxiv.org/abs/2009.03300), [MMLU-Pro](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.01574), [GPQA](https://arxiv.org/abs/2311.12022), [Humanity's Last Exam](https://arxiv.org/abs/2501.14249), [FrontierMath](https://arxiv.org/abs/2411.04872), [Epoch FrontierMath page](https://epoch.ai/frontiermath/the-benchmark).

### Dynamic, live, and contamination-resistant benchmarks

| Benchmark | What it tests | How it is built | How it scores | BenchBench lesson |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| BIG-bench | Broad probing of language model capabilities | Collaborative benchmark with 200+ tasks contributed by many researchers | Task-specific metrics | Community task submission can scale coverage, but quality varies. BenchBench needs task acceptance gates. |
| Dynabench | Robustness under model-in-the-loop data collection | Humans write examples that fool a target model but remain clear to other humans | Task-specific; dynamic rounds | This is the closest ancestor of "models create hard evals." The key constraint is "fool model, not humans." |
| LiveBench | Contamination-free general LLM capabilities | Frequently updated questions from recent math competitions, arXiv papers, news, datasets, and harder variants of prior tasks | Objective ground-truth scoring | Live refresh plus objective grading is one of the cleanest anti-leakage patterns. |
| LiveCodeBench | Code generation and related coding skills | Continuously collects new contest problems from LeetCode, AtCoder, and Codeforces; covers generation, repair, execution, test-output prediction | Functional correctness and task metrics | Time-based sourcing is a practical contamination control. |

Sources: [BIG-bench GitHub](https://github.com/google/BIG-bench), [BIG-bench paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2206.04615), [Dynabench](https://arxiv.org/abs/2104.14337), [LiveBench](https://arxiv.org/abs/2406.19314), [LiveBench GitHub](https://github.com/livebench/livebench), [LiveCodeBench](https://arxiv.org/abs/2403.07974).

### Real-world executable and agent benchmarks

| Benchmark | What it tests | How it is built | How it scores | BenchBench lesson |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| SWE-bench | Real software issue resolution | 2,294 issues and PRs from 12 Python repos; model gets repo plus issue and must edit code | Tests pass after patch | Executable graders are powerful. BenchBench should prefer generated evals with runnable checkers where possible. |
| MLE-bench | Machine learning engineering | 75 Kaggle competitions curated into offline tasks with local train/test splits and grading scripts | Competition-specific score; medal baselines from Kaggle leaderboards | Use existing human competition ecosystems as baselines and graders. |
| RE-Bench | AI R&D / research engineering | METR tasks conforming to a task standard; compares AI agents and human experts under time budgets | Task-specific outcome under controlled budgets | For long-horizon tasks, budget and scaffold must be part of the benchmark definition. |
| OSWorld | Computer-use agents | 369 tasks in real computer environments across desktop/web apps, file I/O, and cross-app workflows | Execution-based task success | Environment setup and reset become part of the benchmark. Generated benchmarks must include reproducible environments. |
| BFCL | Function/tool calling | Real-world functions and multi-turn tool-use scenarios, periodically updated | AST/execution-style correctness, cost | Tool-use benchmarks show the value of narrow, verifiable subskills. |

Sources: [SWE-bench](https://arxiv.org/abs/2310.06770), [SWE-bench GitHub](https://github.com/SWE-bench/SWE-bench), [MLE-bench](https://openai.com/index/mle-bench/), [MLE-bench GitHub](https://github.com/openai/mle-bench), [RE-Bench GitHub](https://github.com/METR/RE-Bench), [METR RE-Bench writeup](https://metr.org/blog/2024-11-22-evaluating-r-d-capabilities-of-llms/), [OSWorld](https://arxiv.org/abs/2404.07972), [BFCL leaderboard](https://gorilla.cs.berkeley.edu/leaderboard), [BFCL project](https://sky.cs.berkeley.edu/project/berkeley-function-calling-leaderboard/).

### Preference, chat, and judge-based benchmarks

| Benchmark | What it tests | How it is built | How it scores | BenchBench lesson |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Chatbot Arena | Human preference over model responses | Blind pairwise comparisons on live user prompts | Elo / Bradley-Terry style ratings from votes | Good for open-ended chat quality, but it measures preference, not ground truth. |
| Arena-Hard | Hard real-user prompts that better predict Arena preference | Samples from Chatbot Arena queries; topic modeling for diversity; LLM filtering for quality | LLM judge / automated preference, checked against Arena agreement | Strong pipeline example: source real prompts, cluster for diversity, filter for quality, validate against human rankings. |
| MT-Bench / LLM-as-judge style evals | Multi-turn helpfulness and instruction following | Fixed prompts with model-judge scoring | Judge scores | Useful for speed, but BenchBench should treat LLM judges as provisional unless calibrated to humans or objective checks. |

Sources: [Chatbot Arena paper](https://arxiv.org/abs/2403.04132), [Arena-Hard pipeline](https://www.lmsys.org/blog/2024-04-19-arena-hard/).

### Benchmark quality and "benchmarking benchmarks"

| Source | Main idea | BenchBench lesson |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Benchmark^2 | Evaluates benchmark quality using cross-benchmark ranking consistency, discriminability, and capability alignment deviation | BenchBench should directly score generated benchmarks on these properties. |
| Bowman and Dahl, "What Will it Take to Fix Benchmarking..." | Benchmarks need validity, reliable annotation, enough statistical power, and attention to social bias | These are acceptance gates before hardness counts. |
| Toward an Evaluation Science for Generative AI Systems | Metrics should map to real-world performance, be iteratively refined, and sit inside institutions/norms | BenchBench should judge whether the benchmark would remain useful outside a one-off paper. |
| tinyBenchmarks / Anchor Points | Item Response Theory can preserve rankings using small high-information item subsets | BenchBench can keep solver costs down by requiring anchor items and item-level difficulty estimates. |

Sources: [Benchmark^2](https://arxiv.org/abs/2601.03986), [Fix Benchmarking in NLU](https://arxiv.org/abs/2104.02145), [Evaluation Science for Generative AI](https://arxiv.org/abs/2503.05336), [tinyBenchmarks](https://arxiv.org/abs/2402.14992), [Anchor Points](https://api.emergentmind.com/papers/2309.08638).

## The eval-correlation material

I found two relevant recent correlation items.

### 1. OpenThoughts3 eval meta-analysis

OpenThoughts3 released results from evaluating about 1,000 models and shows a benchmark-correlation heatmap across reasoning benchmarks. Their main observations:

- rankings across different reasoning benchmarks generally positively correlate
- correlations are stronger within categories, such as math with math or code with code
- some pairs show strong agreement, such as AIME24 and AIME25
- some correlations hide saturation, such as easier math benchmarks where strong models cluster near perfect scores
- Pearson score correlation and Kendall rank correlation can tell different stories, especially when middle-tier models are hard to distinguish
- aggregate rankings can change when the benchmark basket changes; for example, a science-only basket can elevate a different model than an all-category basket

Source: [OpenThoughts3 - 1000 models evaluated](https://www.open-thoughts.ai/blog/ot3-experiment-data).

### 2. "LLM rankings are not a ladder" thread

The recent Reddit thread by Spico197 builds a graph from benchmark wins: if model A beats model B on benchmark X, add edge A -> B. The reported findings:

- 126,937 weak-to-strong model pairs were checked, where the source model had lower Artificial Analysis Intelligence Index than the target
- 119,514 of those pairs were reachable through benchmark win chains, a 94.2% reachable rate
- 91.4% of reachable weak-to-strong paths took only 2-3 hops
- about 119k direct weak-over-strong triples remained after treating non-positive benchmark values as missing
- high-reversal candidates included HLE, IFBench, AIME 2025, TAU2, and SciCode
- IFBench was reported at about 17.5% reversal rate, 80% coverage, and r ~= 0.82 correlation with Intelligence Index

Source: [Reddit thread](https://www.reddit.com/r/MachineLearning/comments/1t8f61o/llm_rankings_are_not_a_ladder_experimental/). The linked tool is [LLM Win](https://llm-win.com/), though the public page did not expose crawlable text in my search session.

### What this means for BenchBench

Do not rank generated benchmarks only by "frontier model failed." A generated benchmark can be valuable in two different ways:

- it aligns with existing capability ladders but is less saturated, cleaner, or cheaper
- it reveals an interpretable residual capability that existing eval baskets miss

BenchBench should therefore measure both:

- consistency: does the generated benchmark produce sensible rankings against nearby evals?
- complementarity: does it add a useful new axis instead of duplicating MMLU/GPQA/AIME/SWE-bench?

Reversals are not automatically bad. A reversal is good if it reflects a named skill specialization and bad if it reflects noise, ambiguous items, bad graders, low coverage, or saturation.

## Proposed BenchBench benchmark package spec

A generator model should output a full package, not just questions:

1. Capability claim
   - What skill does this benchmark measure?
   - Why does the skill matter?
   - What existing evals are adjacent?

2. Task boundary
   - Input format
   - Allowed tools
   - Time/token budget
   - Interaction rules
   - Output format

3. Item set or item generator
   - At least a public dev subset and a private/held-out test subset
   - Provenance for each item
   - Deduplication and contamination checks
   - Difficulty labels or expected difficulty model

4. Grader
   - Objective checker, executable harness, reference answer, calibrated rubric, or human preference protocol
   - Failure cases and ambiguity policy
   - Repeatability requirements

5. Human baseline
   - Who counts as qualified
   - Sample size
   - Time/tool budget
   - Expected score and confidence interval

6. Frontier pre-screen
   - Which solver models were tried
   - Prompt/scaffold budget
   - Best score and uncertainty
   - Evidence that failure is not caused by broken instructions or grading

7. Benchmark-quality report
   - Discriminability
   - Correlation with nearby benchmarks
   - Complementarity / residual skill signal
   - Item-level pass rates
   - Known limitations

## Acceptance gates for generated benchmarks

A BenchBench candidate should pass all gates before getting a hardness score:

1. Validity gate
   - The benchmark measures a named capability, not "stuff the model got wrong."

2. Solvability gate
   - Qualified humans can solve it well above chance. For an MVP, require >= 75% human score or an explained domain-specific threshold.

3. Grading gate
   - The grader is deterministic or has measured inter-rater reliability.

4. Frontier-resistance gate
   - Best tested frontier solver scores below 50% of qualified human performance under the same stated budget.

5. Novelty / contamination gate
   - Items are original, post-cutoff, private, procedurally generated, or checked against known benchmark/training leaks.

6. Statistical gate
   - The benchmark separates at least some solvers with confidence intervals, not just noise.

7. Correlation / complementarity gate
   - The benchmark either tracks a nearby capability better than saturated evals or adds an interpretable new axis.

8. Cost gate
   - A normal run is affordable enough to reproduce, or the benchmark provides a calibrated tiny/anchor subset.

9. Abuse / bias gate
   - The benchmark does not reward harmful behavior, identity shortcuts, or ungrounded cultural assumptions unless those are explicitly the object of study and safely scoped.

## Scoring sketch

Use binary gates first, then score accepted candidates:

```
BenchBenchScore =
  ValidItemCount
  * HumanSolvability
  * FrontierGap
  * GraderReliability
  * Discriminability
  * Complementarity
  * Reproducibility
  - CostPenalty
  - AmbiguityPenalty
  - LeakagePenalty
```

Possible definitions:

- `HumanSolvability`: min(1, human_score / target_human_score)
- `FrontierGap`: max(0, 1 - best_frontier_score / (0.5 * human_score)), capped at 1
- `GraderReliability`: exact checker = 1; human rubric = inter-rater agreement or calibrated judge-human agreement
- `Discriminability`: performance spread adjusted by uncertainty, or IRT item discrimination
- `Complementarity`: residual rank signal after controlling for a benchmark basket, plus an explanation of the skill
- `Reproducibility`: environment rebuild success, deterministic scoring, versioned data

Important: a generated benchmark that no model and no human can solve should score zero, no matter how "hard" it is.

## Suggested MVP

Do a small first run before building a full leaderboard.

1. Ask 5 generator models to produce benchmark packages in 3 domains:
   - short-horizon objective reasoning
   - code/tool/executable tasks
   - domain-expert closed-answer questions

2. Require each generator to produce:
   - 20 public/dev items
   - 50 private/test items or a generator for them
   - grader
   - human baseline plan
   - contamination plan
   - predicted frontier failure mode

3. Run automated validation:
   - schema validation
   - duplicate/leak search
   - prompt clarity check
   - grader determinism check
   - cheap solver pass with 2-3 models

4. Human-review the top 5 generated packages:
   - reject ambiguous tasks
   - repair only formatting/packaging issues, not item logic
   - record review labor as part of the score

5. Run a solver gauntlet:
   - 3-5 frontier solvers
   - fixed prompts/scaffolds
   - multiple seeds where nondeterminism matters
   - item-level outputs saved

6. Publish not only a generator leaderboard, but a benchmark-quality report:
   - how many packages passed gates
   - why packages failed
   - which generated benchmarks were genuinely new/useful
   - whether any exposed a stable residual capability

## Strong initial claim

The defensible paper/project claim is:

> BenchBench evaluates whether frontier models can generate new evaluation instruments that are valid, human-solvable, reliably graded, contamination-resistant, and frontier-resistant.

The stronger claim to avoid until proven:

> Models can autonomously discover the next generation of AI benchmarks.

That may become true, but the first version should prove the narrower thing: which models can produce benchmark candidates that survive real benchmark-construction scrutiny.

# Experiment 001: Three-Model Grid Pilot

This folder preserves the first complete BenchBench pilot grid.

## What It Tested

- Creator models: GPT-5.2, GPT-5.4, GPT-5.5 through Codex.
- Solver models: GPT-5.2, GPT-5.4, GPT-5.5 through Codex.
- Creator prompt style: influenced by the prior Visual Trace success, which
  pulled candidates toward visual/topology benchmarks.

## Main Result

Only the GPT-5.4-created benchmark passed the difficulty gate.

| creator | benchmark | solver GPT-5.2 | solver GPT-5.4 | solver GPT-5.5 | status |
|---|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| GPT-5.2 | Folded Strip Order | 16/30 | 14/30 | 19/30 | too easy |
| GPT-5.4 | Occluded Tile Provenance | 7/30 | 4/30 | 5/30 | passed |
| GPT-5.5 | Shadow Weave Topology | 15/30 | 24/30 | 26/30 | too easy |

Extra sanity check: GPT-5.5 at `xhigh` scored 10/30 on GPT-5.4's candidate.

## Files

- `experiment_summary_three_model_grid_20260515.md`: final interpretation.
- `experiment_summary_two_model_sweep_20260515.md`: earlier two-model sweep.
- `run/`: full run artifacts, candidates, solver outputs, score JSONs, and logs.

## Caveat

This pilot was useful, but the prompt had a visual/topology attractor. The next
experiment should ask for the best possible benchmark in the broadest terms,
provide only benchmark landscape context and prior results, and avoid nudging
toward any specific domain or modality.

private files outside the isolated solver bundle.

+# Failure modes (IgnoreSense)
+
+This benchmark is designed so that naive or partial `.gitignore` implementations fail in characteristic, auditable ways.
+
+## Common solver failures
+
+- **No negation support**: treating `!pattern` as literal text or ignoring it, causing last-rule precedence to be wrong.
+- **Wrong precedence**: using “first match wins” rather than “last match wins”.
+- **Basename semantics wrong**: applying `foo` only to the full path instead of to each path segment.
+- **Anchoring wrong**: treating leading `/` as a literal slash rather than “match from repo root”.
+- **Directory-only wrong**: treating `build/` as matching only the literal directory path, not all files under it.
+- **Escaping wrong**: not handling `\\#` and `\\!` correctly at the start of a pattern.
+- **Glob mistakes**: treating `*` as crossing `/`, or failing to implement `**` correctly.
+
+## Benchmark limitations (intentional scope)
+
+- No nested `.gitignore` files.
+- No `**/` special-casing beyond treating `**` as “match anything including `/`”.
+- No platform path-separator issues: all paths use `/`.
+- No symlinks, filesystem calls, or git attributes.
+
+If you extend this benchmark, expand the subset carefully and keep the reference matcher and solver packet aligned.
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import hashlib
+import json
+import os
+import random
+import re
+from dataclasses import dataclass
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Iterable, List, Optional, Tuple
+
+
+@dataclass(frozen=True)
+class Rule:
+    pattern: str
+    negated: bool
+    directory_only: bool
+    anchored: bool
+    has_slash: bool
+
+
+def _split_gitignore_lines(text: str) -> List[str]:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    for raw in text.splitlines():
+        # Preserve leading spaces (they are significant), but drop trailing \r.
+        line = raw.rstrip("\r")
+        lines.append(line)
+    return lines
+
+
+def parse_gitignore(gitignore_text: str) -> List[Rule]:
+    rules: List[Rule] = []
+    for line in _split_gitignore_lines(gitignore_text):
+        if line == "" or line.lstrip(" ").startswith("#"):
+            continue
+
+        negated = False
+        s = line
+        if s.startswith("!"):
+            negated = True
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        # Escape handling: "\#" and "\!" are literal; "\\" escapes backslash.
+        if s.startswith("\\"):
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        directory_only = s.endswith("/")
+        if directory_only:
+            s = s[:-1]
+
+        anchored = s.startswith("/")
+        if anchored:
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        has_slash = "/" in s
+        if s == "":
+            continue
+
+        rules.append(
+            Rule(
+                pattern=s,
+                negated=negated,
+                directory_only=directory_only,
+                anchored=anchored,
+                has_slash=has_slash,
+            )
+        )
+    return rules
+
+
+_re_special = re.compile(r"([.^$+{}()|\\])")
+
+
+def _glob_to_regex(glob_pat: str) -> re.Pattern[str]:
+    """
+    Translate a restricted gitignore glob pattern into a regex.
+
+    Supported:
+    - "*" matches any string except "/"
+    - "?" matches any single char except "/"
+    - "**" matches any string including "/" (may be empty), but only as a whole
+      path segment token or adjacent to "/" boundaries in our generator.
+    - character classes like "[abc]" or "[a-z]"
+    """
+    i = 0
+    out = ""
+    while i < len(glob_pat):
+        ch = glob_pat[i]
+        if ch == "*":
+            if i + 1 < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[i + 1] == "*":
+                out += ".*"
+                i += 2
+                continue
+            out += "[^/]*"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "?":
+            out += "[^/]"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "[":
+            j = i + 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "!":
+                j += 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "]":
+                j += 1
+            while j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] != "]":
+                j += 1
+            if j >= len(glob_pat):
+                out += r"\["
+                i += 1
+                continue
+            cls = glob_pat[i : j + 1]
+            out += cls
+            i = j + 1
+            continue
+        out += _re_special.sub(r"\\\1", ch)
+        i += 1
+    return re.compile(rf"^{out}$")
+
+
+def _path_segments(path: str) -> List[str]:
+    # Normalize: treat multiple slashes as a single slash; no leading "./".
+    parts = [p for p in path.split("/") if p not in ("", ".")]
+    return parts
+
+
+def _match_rule_to_path(rule: Rule, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    """
+    Implement a well-defined subset of gitignore semantics.
+
+    The matching policy:
+    - All paths are relative and use "/" as separator.
+    - If rule.directory_only is true, it can match a directory path or any file
+      under that directory.
+    - If rule.anchored is true, match is evaluated against the full path from
+      repo root.
+    - If rule.has_slash is false (pattern with no "/"), it can match any
+      single path segment (basename semantics).
+    - If rule.has_slash is true, it matches against the full path string.
+    - Globbing uses the restricted translator above.
+    """
+    segments = _path_segments(path)
+    norm_path = "/".join(segments)
+
+    if norm_path == "":
+        return False
+
+    if rule.has_slash:
+        target = norm_path if rule.anchored else norm_path
+        rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+        matched = rx.match(target) is not None
+        if not matched:
+            return False
+        if rule.directory_only:
+            # If path is dir: ok; if file: ok only if it's under that dir.
+            if is_dir:
+                return True
+            # For directory-only patterns that include slashes, we treat a match
+            # as applying to that directory prefix.
+            return target.startswith(rule.pattern + "/")
+        return True
+
+    # Basename-style: match any segment.
+    rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+    for seg in segments:
+        if rx.match(seg) is not None:
+            if rule.directory_only:
+                # Directory-only basename pattern matches any directory segment,
+                # and therefore ignores the whole subtree.
+                return True
+            return True
+    return False
+
+
+def is_ignored(gitignore_text: str, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    rules = parse_gitignore(gitignore_text)
+    ignored = False
+    for rule in rules:
+        if _match_rule_to_path(rule, path=path, is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored = not rule.negated
+    return ignored
+
+
+def _stable_id(seed: int, idx: int, gitignore_text: str, paths: List[str]) -> str:
+    h = hashlib.sha256()
+    h.update(f"{seed}:{idx}\n".encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(gitignore_text.encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(b"\n")
+    for p in paths:
+        h.update(p.encode("utf-8"))
+        h.update(b"\n")
+    return h.hexdigest()[:16]
+
+
+_SEG_ATOMS = [
+    "src",
+    "lib",
+    "test",
+    "tests",
+    "docs",
+    "build",
+    "dist",
+    "bin",
+    "obj",
+    "tmp",
+    "cache",
+    "node_modules",
+    "vendor",
+    "assets",
+    "data",
+    "out",
+]
+
+_FILE_ATOMS = [
+    "main.py",
+    "app.js",
+    "index.html",
+    "README.md",
+    "notes.txt",
+    "a.out",
+    "report.log",
+    "image.png",
+    "model.bin",
+    "archive.tar",
+    "archive.tar.gz",
+    ".env",
+]
+
+
+def _rand_segment(rng: random.Random) -> str:
+    base = rng.choice(_SEG_ATOMS)
+    if rng.random() < 0.15:
+        base = f"{base}{rng.randint(0, 9)}"
+    if rng.random() < 0.05:
+        base = base.replace("_", "-")
+    return base
+
+
+def _rand_path(rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[str, bool]:
+    depth = rng.randint(1, 4)
+    segs = [_rand_segment(rng) for _ in range(depth - 1)]
+    if rng.random() < 0.30:
+        # Directory path query.
+        segs.append(_rand_segment(rng))
+        return ("/".join(segs) + "/", True)
+    leaf = rng.choice(_FILE_ATOMS)
+    segs.append(leaf)
+    return ("/".join(segs), False)
+
+
+def _pattern_from_path(rng: random.Random, path: str) -> str:
+    # Produce a pattern likely to match the path, with controlled complexity.
+    s = path.rstrip("/")
+    segs = s.split("/")
+    choice = rng.random()
+    if choice < 0.30:
+        # Basename pattern
+        leaf = segs[-1]
+        if rng.random() < 0.35 and "." in leaf:
+            ext = leaf.split(".")[-1]
+            return f"*.{ext}"
+        if rng.random() < 0.20:
+            return leaf[0] + "?" + leaf[2:] if len(leaf) >= 3 else leaf
+        return leaf
+    if choice < 0.65:
+        # Directory pattern
+        d = segs[rng.randint(0, max(0, len(segs) - 2))]
+        return f"{d}/"
+    # Slash-containing pattern
+    prefix_len = rng.randint(1, min(len(segs), 3))
+    prefix = "/".join(segs[:prefix_len])
+    if rng.random() < 0.25:
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/**"
+    if rng.random() < 0.25 and prefix.endswith("**"):
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/*.log"
+    return prefix
+
+
+def _maybe_escape_prefix(rng: random.Random, pat: str) -> str:
+    if pat and pat[0] in ("#", "!") and rng.random() < 0.7:
+        return "\\" + pat
+    return pat
+
+
+def _make_gitignore(rng: random.Random, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    # Add some comments and blank lines
+    if rng.random() < 0.6:
+        lines.append("# IgnoreSense generated gitignore")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        lines.append("")
+
+    # Choose a few patterns derived from paths, plus some distractors.
+    chosen = rng.sample(paths, k=min(len(paths), rng.randint(4, 7)))
+    patterns: List[str] = []
+    for p, _is_dir in chosen:
+        patterns.append(_pattern_from_path(rng, p))
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.tmp")
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.log")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        patterns.append("**/cache/**")
+
+    rng.shuffle(patterns)
+
+    # Add negations to create precedence traps.
+    negations: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns[:]:
+        if rng.random() < 0.25 and not pat.startswith("!"):
+            # Create a negation that partially overlaps
+            if pat.endswith("/"):
+                base = pat[:-1]
+                neg = f"!{base}/keep.*"
+            elif pat.startswith("*."):
+                neg = f"!important{pat[1:]}"
+            else:
+                neg = f"!{pat}"
+            negations.append(neg)
+
+    # Build final lines with occasional anchoring.
+    all_lines: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns + negations:
+        p = pat
+        if not p.startswith(("!", "\\")) and rng.random() < 0.2:
+            p = "/" + p
+        p = _maybe_escape_prefix(rng, p)
+        all_lines.append(p)
+
+    # Ensure at least one negation and one directory-only pattern in most items.
+    if not any(l.startswith("!") for l in all_lines):
+        all_lines.append("!README.md")
+    if not any(l.rstrip("\n").rstrip("\r").endswith("/") for l in all_lines if not l.startswith("#")):
+        all_lines.append("build/")
+
+    # Intermix some spacing and comment quirks
+    out: List[str] = []
+    for l in all_lines:
+        if rng.random() < 0.15:
+            out.append("  " + l)
+        else:
+            out.append(l)
+        if rng.random() < 0.10:
+            out.append("# trailing comment line")
+    return "\n".join(out) + "\n"
+
+
+def _compute_answer(gitignore_text: str, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    ignored: List[str] = []
+    for p, is_dir in paths:
+        if is_ignored(gitignore_text, p.rstrip("/"), is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored.append(p)
+    ignored_sorted = sorted(ignored)
+    return json.dumps(ignored_sorted, ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",", ":"))
+
+
+def _write_jsonl(path: Path, rows: Iterable[dict]) -> None:
+    with path.open("w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for row in rows:
+            f.write(json.dumps(row, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n")
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--sample-count", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--seed", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--out-dir", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    out_dir = Path(args.out_dir)
+    out_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+    solver_dir = out_dir / "solver_bundle"
+    solver_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+
+    rng = random.Random(args.seed)
+
+    items_rows: List[dict] = []
+    gold_rows: List[dict] = []
+
+    for idx in range(args.sample_count):
+        # Create candidate paths with some duplicates removed.
+        raw_paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]] = []
+        while len(raw_paths) < 12:
+            p, is_dir = _rand_path(rng)
+            if (p, is_dir) not in raw_paths:
+                raw_paths.append((p, is_dir))
+
+        gitignore_text = _make_gitignore(rng, raw_paths)
+        paths_only = [p for p, _ in raw_paths]
+        item_id = _stable_id(args.seed, idx, gitignore_text, paths_only)
+
+        answer = _compute_answer(gitignore_text, raw_paths)
+        items_rows.append(
+            {
+                "id": item_id,
+                "gitignore": gitignore_text,
+                "paths": paths_only,
+            }
+        )
+        gold_rows.append({"id": item_id, "answer": answer})
+
+    _write_jsonl(solver_dir / "items_private_sample.jsonl", items_rows)
+    _write_jsonl(out_dir / "gold_private_sample.jsonl", gold_rows)
+
+    manifest = {
+        "benchmark_name": "IgnoreSense",
+        "benchmark_version": "1.0.0",
+        "items_file": "items_private_sample.jsonl",
+        "answer_format": "JSON array of ignored paths sorted lexicographically; answer is serialized as a compact JSON string.",
+        "notes": [
+            "All tasks are self-contained; do not assume full gitignore semantics beyond what the packet describes.",
+            "Paths use '/' separators and are relative (no leading './'). Directory paths end with '/'.",
+        ],
+    }
+    (solver_dir / "SOLVER_MANIFEST.json").write_text(
+        json.dumps(manifest, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n", encoding="utf-8"
+    )
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import json
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Dict, List, Tuple
+
+
+def _read_jsonl_exact_keys(path: Path, required_keys: Tuple[str, str]) -> List[dict]:
+    rows: List[dict] = []
+    with path.open("r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for line in f:
+            line = line.strip()
+            if not line:
+                continue
+            obj = json.loads(line)
+            if set(obj.keys()) != set(required_keys):
+                raise SystemExit(f"Row keys must be exactly {set(required_keys)} in {path}: {obj.keys()}")
+            rows.append(obj)
+    return rows
+
+
+def _normalize_answer(ans: str) -> str:
+    # Parse as JSON array of strings, sort, and dump compactly.
+    try:
+        arr = json.loads(ans)
+    except Exception as e:
+        raise ValueError(f"answer is not valid JSON: {e}")
+    if not isinstance(arr, list) or not all(isinstance(x, str) for x in arr):
+        raise ValueError("answer must be a JSON array of strings")
+    arr_sorted = sorted(arr)
+    return json.dumps(arr_sorted, ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",", ":"))
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--gold", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--predictions", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--out", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    gold_rows = _read_jsonl_exact_keys(Path(args.gold), ("id", "answer"))
+    pred_rows = _read_jsonl_exact_keys(Path(args.predictions), ("id", "answer"))
+
+    gold_map: Dict[str, str] = {r["id"]: r["answer"] for r in gold_rows}
+    if len(gold_map) != len(gold_rows):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate gold ids found.")
+
+    pred_map: Dict[str, str] = {r["id"]: r["answer"] for r in pred_rows}
+    if len(pred_map) != len(pred_rows):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate prediction ids found.")
+
+    missing = sorted(set(gold_map.keys()) - set(pred_map.keys()))
+    extra = sorted(set(pred_map.keys()) - set(gold_map.keys()))
+
+    correct = 0
+    total = len(gold_map)
+    per_item: List[dict] = []
+    invalid_answers: List[str] = []
+
+    for item_id in sorted(gold_map.keys()):
+        if item_id not in pred_map:
+            per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": False, "reason": "missing_prediction"})
+            continue
+        gold_norm = _normalize_answer(gold_map[item_id])
+        try:
+            pred_norm = _normalize_answer(pred_map[item_id])
+        except Exception as e:
+            invalid_answers.append(item_id)
+            per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": False, "reason": f"invalid_answer:{e}"})
+            continue
+        ok = pred_norm == gold_norm
+        if ok:
+            correct += 1
+        per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": ok})
+
+    report = {
+        "total": total,
+        "correct": correct,
+        "accuracy": (correct / total) if total else 0.0,
+        "missing_predictions": missing,
+        "extra_predictions": extra,
+        "invalid_answer_ids": invalid_answers,
+        "per_item": per_item,
+    }
+    Path(args.out).write_text(json.dumps(report, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")
+    print(json.dumps({"accuracy": report["accuracy"], "correct": correct, "total": total}))
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+# IgnoreSense solver packet
+
+You are given a set of independent items. Each item contains:
+
+- `gitignore`: the contents of a `.gitignore` file (single file, no nested `.gitignore`s)
+- `paths`: a list of relative paths to classify as ignored vs not ignored
+
+Your job is to output `predictions.jsonl` with **exactly**:
+
+```json
+{"id":"...","answer":"..."}
+```
+
+Where `answer` is a **string** that is itself a JSON array of strings: the paths from `paths` that are ignored, sorted lexicographically.
+
+Example answer string:
+
+```json
+"[\"build/\",\"dist/app.js\"]"
+```
+
+## Matching semantics (the subset used in this benchmark)
+
+This benchmark uses a precise subset of `.gitignore` semantics, implemented by the reference matcher used to generate the gold answers.
+
+### Line handling
+
+- Blank lines are ignored.
+- Lines whose first non-space character is `#` are comments and ignored.
+- A leading `!` negates a pattern (un-ignore). Last matching rule wins.
+- A leading `\\` escapes the next character so that `\\#` and `\\!` match literal `#` and `!` at the start.
+
+### Pattern handling
+
+Patterns are matched against each query path using `/` as separator:
+
+- A trailing `/` makes a pattern **directory-only**: if it matches a directory, it ignores the entire directory subtree.
+- A leading `/` anchors a pattern to the repo root (all paths are already relative).
+- If the pattern contains no `/`, it is a **basename** pattern and is tested against each path segment.
+- If the pattern contains `/`, it is tested against the full normalized path.
+
+### Globs
+
+- `*` matches any string except `/`
+- `?` matches any single character except `/`
+- `**` matches any string including `/` (may be empty)
+- Character classes like `[abc]` and `[a-z]` are supported
+
+Important: do not assume additional gitignore features beyond the above subset.
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import json
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Dict, List, Tuple
+
+from generator import _compute_answer
+
+
+def _read_jsonl(path: Path) -> List[dict]:
+    rows: List[dict] = []
+    with path.open("r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for line in f:
+            line = line.strip()
+            if not line:
+                continue
+            rows.append(json.loads(line))
+    return rows
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--items", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--gold", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    items_path = Path(args.items)
+    gold_path = Path(args.gold)
+
+    items = _read_jsonl(items_path)
+    gold = _read_jsonl(gold_path)
+
+    gold_map: Dict[str, str] = {}
+    for row in gold:
+        if set(row.keys()) != {"id", "answer"}:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Gold row keys must be exactly {{id, answer}}: {row.keys()}")
+        gold_map[row["id"]] = row["answer"]
+
+    if len(gold_map) != len(gold):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate gold ids found.")
+
+    for item in items:
+        if set(item.keys()) != {"id", "gitignore", "paths"}:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Item row keys must be exactly {{id, gitignore, paths}}: {item.keys()}")
+        item_id = item["id"]
+        if item_id not in gold_map:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Item id missing from gold: {item_id}")
+        if not isinstance(item["paths"], list) or not all(isinstance(p, str) for p in item["paths"]):
+            raise SystemExit(f"Invalid paths list for item {item_id}")
+
+        # Recompute expected answer from solver-visible fields and compare.
+        # Treat directory paths by trailing '/' convention in the item payload.
+        raw_paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]] = []
+        for p in item["paths"]:
+            raw_paths.append((p, p.endswith("/")))
+        expected = _compute_answer(item["gitignore"], raw_paths)
+        if expected != gold_map[item_id]:
+            raise SystemExit(
+                f"Gold mismatch for id={item_id}: recomputed={expected} gold={gold_map[item_id]}"
+            )
+
+    if set(gold_map.keys()) != {i["id"] for i in items}:
+        raise SystemExit("Gold ids and item ids do not match exactly.")
+
+    print("OK: items match gold under reference matcher.")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+# Failure modes (IgnoreSense)
+
+This benchmark is designed so that naive or partial `.gitignore` implementations fail in characteristic, auditable ways.
+
+## Common solver failures
+
+- **No negation support**: treating `!pattern` as literal text or ignoring it, causing last-rule precedence to be wrong.
+- **Wrong precedence**: using “first match wins” rather than “last match wins”.
+- **Basename semantics wrong**: applying `foo` only to the full path instead of to each path segment.
+- **Anchoring wrong**: treating leading `/` as a literal slash rather than “match from repo root”.
+- **Directory-only wrong**: treating `build/` as matching only the literal directory path, not all files under it.
+- **Escaping wrong**: not handling `\\#` and `\\!` correctly at the start of a pattern.
+- **Glob mistakes**: treating `*` as crossing `/`, or failing to implement `**` correctly.
+
+## Benchmark limitations (intentional scope)
+
+- No nested `.gitignore` files.
+- No `**/` special-casing beyond treating `**` as “match anything including `/`”.
+- No platform path-separator issues: all paths use `/`.
+- No symlinks, filesystem calls, or git attributes.
+
+If you extend this benchmark, expand the subset carefully and keep the reference matcher and solver packet aligned.
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import hashlib
+import json
+import os
+import random
+import re
+from dataclasses import dataclass
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Iterable, List, Optional, Tuple
+
+
+@dataclass(frozen=True)
+class Rule:
+    pattern: str
+    negated: bool
+    directory_only: bool
+    anchored: bool
+    has_slash: bool
+
+
+def _split_gitignore_lines(text: str) -> List[str]:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    for raw in text.splitlines():
+        # Preserve leading spaces (they are significant), but drop trailing \r.
+        line = raw.rstrip("\r")
+        lines.append(line)
+    return lines
+
+
+def parse_gitignore(gitignore_text: str) -> List[Rule]:
+    rules: List[Rule] = []
+    for line in _split_gitignore_lines(gitignore_text):
+        if line == "" or line.lstrip(" ").startswith("#"):
+            continue
+
+        negated = False
+        s = line
+        if s.startswith("!"):
+            negated = True
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        # Escape handling: "\#" and "\!" are literal; "\\" escapes backslash.
+        if s.startswith("\\"):
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        directory_only = s.endswith("/")
+        if directory_only:
+            s = s[:-1]
+
+        anchored = s.startswith("/")
+        if anchored:
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        has_slash = "/" in s
+        if s == "":
+            continue
+
+        rules.append(
+            Rule(
+                pattern=s,
+                negated=negated,
+                directory_only=directory_only,
+                anchored=anchored,
+                has_slash=has_slash,
+            )
+        )
+    return rules
+
+
+_re_special = re.compile(r"([.^$+{}()|\\])")
+
+
+def _glob_to_regex(glob_pat: str) -> re.Pattern[str]:
+    """
+    Translate a restricted gitignore glob pattern into a regex.
+
+    Supported:
+    - "*" matches any string except "/"
+    - "?" matches any single char except "/"
+    - "**" matches any string including "/" (may be empty), but only as a whole
+      path segment token or adjacent to "/" boundaries in our generator.
+    - character classes like "[abc]" or "[a-z]"
+    """
+    i = 0
+    out = ""
+    while i < len(glob_pat):
+        ch = glob_pat[i]
+        if ch == "*":
+            if i + 1 < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[i + 1] == "*":
+                out += ".*"
+                i += 2
+                continue
+            out += "[^/]*"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "?":
+            out += "[^/]"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "[":
+            j = i + 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "!":
+                j += 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "]":
+                j += 1
+            while j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] != "]":
+                j += 1
+            if j >= len(glob_pat):
+                out += r"\["
+                i += 1
+                continue
+            cls = glob_pat[i : j + 1]
+            out += cls
+            i = j + 1
+            continue
+        out += _re_special.sub(r"\\\1", ch)
+        i += 1
+    return re.compile(rf"^{out}$")
+
+
+def _path_segments(path: str) -> List[str]:
+    # Normalize: treat multiple slashes as a single slash; no leading "./".
+    parts = [p for p in path.split("/") if p not in ("", ".")]
+    return parts
+
+
+def _match_rule_to_path(rule: Rule, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    """
+    Implement a well-defined subset of gitignore semantics.
+
+    The matching policy:
+    - All paths are relative and use "/" as separator.
+    - If rule.directory_only is true, it can match a directory path or any file
+      under that directory.
+    - If rule.anchored is true, match is evaluated against the full path from
+      repo root.
+    - If rule.has_slash is false (pattern with no "/"), it can match any
+      single path segment (basename semantics).
+    - If rule.has_slash is true, it matches against the full path string.
+    - Globbing uses the restricted translator above.
+    """
+    segments = _path_segments(path)
+    norm_path = "/".join(segments)
+
+    if norm_path == "":
+        return False
+
+    if rule.has_slash:
+        target = norm_path if rule.anchored else norm_path
+        rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+        matched = rx.match(target) is not None
+        if not matched:
+            return False
+        if rule.directory_only:
+            # If path is dir: ok; if file: ok only if it's under that dir.
+            if is_dir:
+                return True
+            # For directory-only patterns that include slashes, we treat a match
+            # as applying to that directory prefix.
+            return target.startswith(rule.pattern + "/")
+        return True
+
+    # Basename-style: match any segment.
+    rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+    for seg in segments:
+        if rx.match(seg) is not None:
+            if rule.directory_only:
+                # Directory-only basename pattern matches any directory segment,
+                # and therefore ignores the whole subtree.
+                return True
+            return True
+    return False
+
+
+def is_ignored(gitignore_text: str, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    rules = parse_gitignore(gitignore_text)
+    ignored = False
+    for rule in rules:
+        if _match_rule_to_path(rule, path=path, is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored = not rule.negated
+    return ignored
+
+
+def _stable_id(seed: int, idx: int, gitignore_text: str, paths: List[str]) -> str:
+    h = hashlib.sha256()
+    h.update(f"{seed}:{idx}\n".encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(gitignore_text.encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(b"\n")
+    for p in paths:
+        h.update(p.encode("utf-8"))
+        h.update(b"\n")
+    return h.hexdigest()[:16]
+
+
+_SEG_ATOMS = [
+    "src",
+    "lib",
+    "test",
+    "tests",
+    "docs",
+    "build",
+    "dist",
+    "bin",
+    "obj",
+    "tmp",
+    "cache",
+    "node_modules",
+    "vendor",
+    "assets",
+    "data",
+    "out",
+]
+
+_FILE_ATOMS = [
+    "main.py",
+    "app.js",
+    "index.html",
+    "README.md",
+    "notes.txt",
+    "a.out",
+    "report.log",
+    "image.png",
+    "model.bin",
+    "archive.tar",
+    "archive.tar.gz",
+    ".env",
+]
+
+
+def _rand_segment(rng: random.Random) -> str:
+    base = rng.choice(_SEG_ATOMS)
+    if rng.random() < 0.15:
+        base = f"{base}{rng.randint(0, 9)}"
+    if rng.random() < 0.05:
+        base = base.replace("_", "-")
+    return base
+
+
+def _rand_path(rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[str, bool]:
+    depth = rng.randint(1, 4)
+    segs = [_rand_segment(rng) for _ in range(depth - 1)]
+    if rng.random() < 0.30:
+        # Directory path query.
+        segs.append(_rand_segment(rng))
+        return ("/".join(segs) + "/", True)
+    leaf = rng.choice(_FILE_ATOMS)
+    segs.append(leaf)
+    return ("/".join(segs), False)
+
+
+def _pattern_from_path(rng: random.Random, path: str) -> str:
+    # Produce a pattern likely to match the path, with controlled complexity.
+    s = path.rstrip("/")
+    segs = s.split("/")
+    choice = rng.random()
+    if choice < 0.30:
+        # Basename pattern
+        leaf = segs[-1]
+        if rng.random() < 0.35 and "." in leaf:
+            ext = leaf.split(".")[-1]
+            return f"*.{ext}"
+        if rng.random() < 0.20:
+            return leaf[0] + "?" + leaf[2:] if len(leaf) >= 3 else leaf
+        return leaf
+    if choice < 0.65:
+        # Directory pattern
+        d = segs[rng.randint(0, max(0, len(segs) - 2))]
+        return f"{d}/"
+    # Slash-containing pattern
+    prefix_len = rng.randint(1, min(len(segs), 3))
+    prefix = "/".join(segs[:prefix_len])
+    if rng.random() < 0.25:
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/**"
+    if rng.random() < 0.25 and prefix.endswith("**"):
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/*.log"
+    return prefix
+
+
+def _maybe_escape_prefix(rng: random.Random, pat: str) -> str:
+    if pat and pat[0] in ("#", "!") and rng.random() < 0.7:
+        return "\\" + pat
+    return pat
+
+
+def _make_gitignore(rng: random.Random, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    # Add some comments and blank lines
+    if rng.random() < 0.6:
+        lines.append("# IgnoreSense generated gitignore")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        lines.append("")
+
+    # Choose a few patterns derived from paths, plus some distractors.
+    chosen = rng.sample(paths, k=min(len(paths), rng.randint(4, 7)))
+    patterns: List[str] = []
+    for p, _is_dir in chosen:
+        patterns.append(_pattern_from_path(rng, p))
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.tmp")
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.log")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        patterns.append("**/cache/**")
+
+    rng.shuffle(patterns)
+
+    # Add negations to create precedence traps.
+    negations: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns[:]:
+        if rng.random() < 0.25 and not pat.startswith("!"):
+            # Create a negation that partially overlaps
+            if pat.endswith("/"):
+                base = pat[:-1]
+                neg = f"!{base}/keep.*"
+            elif pat.startswith("*."):
+                neg = f"!important{pat[1:]}"
+            else:
+                neg = f"!{pat}"
+            negations.append(neg)
+
+    # Build final lines with occasional anchoring.
+    all_lines: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns + negations:
+        p = pat
+        if not p.startswith(("!", "\\")) and rng.random() < 0.2:
+            p = "/" + p
+        p = _maybe_escape_prefix(rng, p)
+        all_lines.append(p)
+
+    # Ensure at least one negation and one directory-only pattern in most items.
+    if not any(l.startswith("!") for l in all_lines):
+        all_lines.append("!README.md")
+    if not any(l.rstrip("\n").rstrip("\r").endswith("/") for l in all_lines if not l.startswith("#")):
+        all_lines.append("build/")
+
+    # Intermix some spacing and comment quirks
+    out: List[str] = []
+    for l in all_lines:
+        if rng.random() < 0.15:
+            out.append("  " + l)
+        else:
+            out.append(l)
+        if rng.random() < 0.10:
+            out.append("# trailing comment line")
+    return "\n".join(out) + "\n"
+
+
+def _compute_answer(gitignore_text: str, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    ignored: List[str] = []
+    for p, is_dir in paths:
+        if is_ignored(gitignore_text, p.rstrip("/"), is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored.append(p)
+    ignored_sorted = sorted(ignored)
+    return json.dumps(ignored_sorted, ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",", ":"))
+
+
+def _write_jsonl(path: Path, rows: Iterable[dict]) -> None:
+    with path.open("w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for row in rows:
+            f.write(json.dumps(row, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n")
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--sample-count", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--seed", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--out-dir", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    out_dir = Path(args.out_dir)
+    out_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+    solver_dir = out_dir / "solver_bundle"
+    solver_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+
+    rng = random.Random(args.seed)
+
+    items_rows: List[dict] = []
+    gold_rows: List[dict] = []
+
+    for idx in range(args.sample_count):
+        # Create candidate paths with some duplicates removed.
+        raw_paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]] = []
+        while len(raw_paths) < 12:
+            p, is_dir = _rand_path(rng)
+            if (p, is_dir) not in raw_paths:
+                raw_paths.append((p, is_dir))
+
+        gitignore_text = _make_gitignore(rng, raw_paths)
+        paths_only = [p for p, _ in raw_paths]
+        item_id = _stable_id(args.seed, idx, gitignore_text, paths_only)
+
+        answer = _compute_answer(gitignore_text, raw_paths)
+        items_rows.append(
+            {
+                "id": item_id,
+                "gitignore": gitignore_text,
+                "paths": paths_only,
+            }
+        )
+        gold_rows.append({"id": item_id, "answer": answer})
+
+    _write_jsonl(solver_dir / "items_private_sample.jsonl", items_rows)
+    _write_jsonl(out_dir / "gold_private_sample.jsonl", gold_rows)
+
+    manifest = {
+        "benchmark_name": "IgnoreSense",
+        "benchmark_version": "1.0.0",
+        "items_file": "items_private_sample.jsonl",
+        "answer_format": "JSON array of ignored paths sorted lexicographically; answer is serialized as a compact JSON string.",
+        "notes": [
+            "All tasks are self-contained; do not assume full gitignore semantics beyond what the packet describes.",
+            "Paths use '/' separators and are relative (no leading './'). Directory paths end with '/'.",
+        ],
+    }
+    (solver_dir / "SOLVER_MANIFEST.json").write_text(
+        json.dumps(manifest, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n", encoding="utf-8"
+    )
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import json
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Dict, List, Tuple
+
+
+def _read_jsonl_exact_keys(path: Path, required_keys: Tuple[str, str]) -> List[dict]:
+    rows: List[dict] = []
+    with path.open("r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for line in f:
+            line = line.strip()
+            if not line:
+                continue
+            obj = json.loads(line)
+            if set(obj.keys()) != set(required_keys):
+                raise SystemExit(f"Row keys must be exactly {set(required_keys)} in {path}: {obj.keys()}")
+            rows.append(obj)
+    return rows
+
+
+def _normalize_answer(ans: str) -> str:
+    # Parse as JSON array of strings, sort, and dump compactly.
+    try:
+        arr = json.loads(ans)
+    except Exception as e:
+        raise ValueError(f"answer is not valid JSON: {e}")
+    if not isinstance(arr, list) or not all(isinstance(x, str) for x in arr):
+        raise ValueError("answer must be a JSON array of strings")
+    arr_sorted = sorted(arr)
+    return json.dumps(arr_sorted, ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",", ":"))
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--gold", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--predictions", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--out", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    gold_rows = _read_jsonl_exact_keys(Path(args.gold), ("id", "answer"))
+    pred_rows = _read_jsonl_exact_keys(Path(args.predictions), ("id", "answer"))
+
+    gold_map: Dict[str, str] = {r["id"]: r["answer"] for r in gold_rows}
+    if len(gold_map) != len(gold_rows):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate gold ids found.")
+
+    pred_map: Dict[str, str] = {r["id"]: r["answer"] for r in pred_rows}
+    if len(pred_map) != len(pred_rows):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate prediction ids found.")
+
+    missing = sorted(set(gold_map.keys()) - set(pred_map.keys()))
+    extra = sorted(set(pred_map.keys()) - set(gold_map.keys()))
+
+    correct = 0
+    total = len(gold_map)
+    per_item: List[dict] = []
+    invalid_answers: List[str] = []
+
+    for item_id in sorted(gold_map.keys()):
+        if item_id not in pred_map:
+            per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": False, "reason": "missing_prediction"})
+            continue
+        gold_norm = _normalize_answer(gold_map[item_id])
+        try:
+            pred_norm = _normalize_answer(pred_map[item_id])
+        except Exception as e:
+            invalid_answers.append(item_id)
+            per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": False, "reason": f"invalid_answer:{e}"})
+            continue
+        ok = pred_norm == gold_norm
+        if ok:
+            correct += 1
+        per_item.append({"id": item_id, "correct": ok})
+
+    report = {
+        "total": total,
+        "correct": correct,
+        "accuracy": (correct / total) if total else 0.0,
+        "missing_predictions": missing,
+        "extra_predictions": extra,
+        "invalid_answer_ids": invalid_answers,
+        "per_item": per_item,
+    }
+    Path(args.out).write_text(json.dumps(report, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n", encoding="utf-8")
+    print(json.dumps({"accuracy": report["accuracy"], "correct": correct, "total": total}))
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+# IgnoreSense solver packet
+
+You are given a set of independent items. Each item contains:
+
+- `gitignore`: the contents of a `.gitignore` file (single file, no nested `.gitignore`s)
+- `paths`: a list of relative paths to classify as ignored vs not ignored
+
+Your job is to output `predictions.jsonl` with **exactly**:
+
+```json
+{"id":"...","answer":"..."}
+```
+
+Where `answer` is a **string** that is itself a JSON array of strings: the paths from `paths` that are ignored, sorted lexicographically.
+
+Example answer string:
+
+```json
+"[\"build/\",\"dist/app.js\"]"
+```
+
+## Matching semantics (the subset used in this benchmark)
+
+This benchmark uses a precise subset of `.gitignore` semantics, implemented by the reference matcher used to generate the gold answers.
+
+### Line handling
+
+- Blank lines are ignored.
+- Lines whose first non-space character is `#` are comments and ignored.
+- A leading `!` negates a pattern (un-ignore). Last matching rule wins.
+- A leading `\\` escapes the next character so that `\\#` and `\\!` match literal `#` and `!` at the start.
+
+### Pattern handling
+
+Patterns are matched against each query path using `/` as separator:
+
+- A trailing `/` makes a pattern **directory-only**: if it matches a directory, it ignores the entire directory subtree.
+- A leading `/` anchors a pattern to the repo root (all paths are already relative).
+- If the pattern contains no `/`, it is a **basename** pattern and is tested against each path segment.
+- If the pattern contains `/`, it is tested against the full normalized path.
+
+### Globs
+
+- `*` matches any string except `/`
+- `?` matches any single character except `/`
+- `**` matches any string including `/` (may be empty)
+- Character classes like `[abc]` and `[a-z]` are supported
+
+Important: do not assume additional gitignore features beyond the above subset.
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import json
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Dict, List, Tuple
+
+from generator import _compute_answer
+
+
+def _read_jsonl(path: Path) -> List[dict]:
+    rows: List[dict] = []
+    with path.open("r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for line in f:
+            line = line.strip()
+            if not line:
+                continue
+            rows.append(json.loads(line))
+    return rows
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--items", type=str, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--gold", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    items_path = Path(args.items)
+    gold_path = Path(args.gold)
+
+    items = _read_jsonl(items_path)
+    gold = _read_jsonl(gold_path)
+
+    gold_map: Dict[str, str] = {}
+    for row in gold:
+        if set(row.keys()) != {"id", "answer"}:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Gold row keys must be exactly {{id, answer}}: {row.keys()}")
+        gold_map[row["id"]] = row["answer"]
+
+    if len(gold_map) != len(gold):
+        raise SystemExit("Duplicate gold ids found.")
+
+    for item in items:
+        if set(item.keys()) != {"id", "gitignore", "paths"}:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Item row keys must be exactly {{id, gitignore, paths}}: {item.keys()}")
+        item_id = item["id"]
+        if item_id not in gold_map:
+            raise SystemExit(f"Item id missing from gold: {item_id}")
+        if not isinstance(item["paths"], list) or not all(isinstance(p, str) for p in item["paths"]):
+            raise SystemExit(f"Invalid paths list for item {item_id}")
+
+        # Recompute expected answer from solver-visible fields and compare.
+        # Treat directory paths by trailing '/' convention in the item payload.
+        raw_paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]] = []
+        for p in item["paths"]:
+            raw_paths.append((p, p.endswith("/")))
+        expected = _compute_answer(item["gitignore"], raw_paths)
+        if expected != gold_map[item_id]:
+            raise SystemExit(
+                f"Gold mismatch for id={item_id}: recomputed={expected} gold={gold_map[item_id]}"
+            )
+
+    if set(gold_map.keys()) != {i["id"] for i in items}:
+        raise SystemExit("Gold ids and item ids do not match exactly.")
+
+    print("OK: items match gold under reference matcher.")
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+

+# Failure modes (IgnoreSense)
+
+This benchmark is designed so that naive or partial `.gitignore` implementations fail in characteristic, auditable ways.
+
+## Common solver failures
+
+- **No negation support**: treating `!pattern` as literal text or ignoring it, causing last-rule precedence to be wrong.
+- **Wrong precedence**: using “first match wins” rather than “last match wins”.
+- **Basename semantics wrong**: applying `foo` only to the full path instead of to each path segment.
+- **Anchoring wrong**: treating leading `/` as a literal slash rather than “match from repo root”.
+- **Directory-only wrong**: treating `build/` as matching only the literal directory path, not all files under it.
+- **Escaping wrong**: not handling `\\#` and `\\!` correctly at the start of a pattern.
+- **Glob mistakes**: treating `*` as crossing `/`, or failing to implement `**` correctly.
+
+## Benchmark limitations (intentional scope)
+
+- No nested `.gitignore` files.
+- No `**/` special-casing beyond treating `**` as “match anything including `/`”.
+- No platform path-separator issues: all paths use `/`.
+- No symlinks, filesystem calls, or git attributes.
+
+If you extend this benchmark, expand the subset carefully and keep the reference matcher and solver packet aligned.
+

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import argparse
+import hashlib
+import json
+import os
+import random
+import re
+from dataclasses import dataclass
+from pathlib import Path
+from typing import Iterable, List, Optional, Tuple
+
+
+@dataclass(frozen=True)
+class Rule:
+    pattern: str
+    negated: bool
+    directory_only: bool
+    anchored: bool
+    has_slash: bool
+
+
+def _split_gitignore_lines(text: str) -> List[str]:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    for raw in text.splitlines():
+        # Preserve leading spaces (they are significant), but drop trailing \r.
+        line = raw.rstrip("\r")
+        lines.append(line)
+    return lines
+
+
+def parse_gitignore(gitignore_text: str) -> List[Rule]:
+    rules: List[Rule] = []
+    for line in _split_gitignore_lines(gitignore_text):
+        if line == "" or line.lstrip(" ").startswith("#"):
+            continue
+
+        negated = False
+        s = line
+        if s.startswith("!"):
+            negated = True
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        # Escape handling: "\#" and "\!" are literal; "\\" escapes backslash.
+        if s.startswith("\\"):
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        directory_only = s.endswith("/")
+        if directory_only:
+            s = s[:-1]
+
+        anchored = s.startswith("/")
+        if anchored:
+            s = s[1:]
+
+        has_slash = "/" in s
+        if s == "":
+            continue
+
+        rules.append(
+            Rule(
+                pattern=s,
+                negated=negated,
+                directory_only=directory_only,
+                anchored=anchored,
+                has_slash=has_slash,
+            )
+        )
+    return rules
+
+
+_re_special = re.compile(r"([.^$+{}()|\\])")
+
+
+def _glob_to_regex(glob_pat: str) -> re.Pattern[str]:
+    """
+    Translate a restricted gitignore glob pattern into a regex.
+
+    Supported:
+    - "*" matches any string except "/"
+    - "?" matches any single char except "/"
+    - "**" matches any string including "/" (may be empty), but only as a whole
+      path segment token or adjacent to "/" boundaries in our generator.
+    - character classes like "[abc]" or "[a-z]"
+    """
+    i = 0
+    out = ""
+    while i < len(glob_pat):
+        ch = glob_pat[i]
+        if ch == "*":
+            if i + 1 < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[i + 1] == "*":
+                out += ".*"
+                i += 2
+                continue
+            out += "[^/]*"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "?":
+            out += "[^/]"
+            i += 1
+            continue
+        if ch == "[":
+            j = i + 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "!":
+                j += 1
+            if j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] == "]":
+                j += 1
+            while j < len(glob_pat) and glob_pat[j] != "]":
+                j += 1
+            if j >= len(glob_pat):
+                out += r"\["
+                i += 1
+                continue
+            cls = glob_pat[i : j + 1]
+            out += cls
+            i = j + 1
+            continue
+        out += _re_special.sub(r"\\\1", ch)
+        i += 1
+    return re.compile(rf"^{out}$")
+
+
+def _path_segments(path: str) -> List[str]:
+    # Normalize: treat multiple slashes as a single slash; no leading "./".
+    parts = [p for p in path.split("/") if p not in ("", ".")]
+    return parts
+
+
+def _match_rule_to_path(rule: Rule, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    """
+    Implement a well-defined subset of gitignore semantics.
+
+    The matching policy:
+    - All paths are relative and use "/" as separator.
+    - If rule.directory_only is true, it can match a directory path or any file
+      under that directory.
+    - If rule.anchored is true, match is evaluated against the full path from
+      repo root.
+    - If rule.has_slash is false (pattern with no "/"), it can match any
+      single path segment (basename semantics).
+    - If rule.has_slash is true, it matches against the full path string.
+    - Globbing uses the restricted translator above.
+    """
+    segments = _path_segments(path)
+    norm_path = "/".join(segments)
+
+    if norm_path == "":
+        return False
+
+    if rule.has_slash:
+        target = norm_path if rule.anchored else norm_path
+        rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+        matched = rx.match(target) is not None
+        if not matched:
+            return False
+        if rule.directory_only:
+            # If path is dir: ok; if file: ok only if it's under that dir.
+            if is_dir:
+                return True
+            # For directory-only patterns that include slashes, we treat a match
+            # as applying to that directory prefix.
+            return target.startswith(rule.pattern + "/")
+        return True
+
+    # Basename-style: match any segment.
+    rx = _glob_to_regex(rule.pattern)
+    for seg in segments:
+        if rx.match(seg) is not None:
+            if rule.directory_only:
+                # Directory-only basename pattern matches any directory segment,
+                # and therefore ignores the whole subtree.
+                return True
+            return True
+    return False
+
+
+def is_ignored(gitignore_text: str, path: str, is_dir: bool) -> bool:
+    rules = parse_gitignore(gitignore_text)
+    ignored = False
+    for rule in rules:
+        if _match_rule_to_path(rule, path=path, is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored = not rule.negated
+    return ignored
+
+
+def _stable_id(seed: int, idx: int, gitignore_text: str, paths: List[str]) -> str:
+    h = hashlib.sha256()
+    h.update(f"{seed}:{idx}\n".encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(gitignore_text.encode("utf-8"))
+    h.update(b"\n")
+    for p in paths:
+        h.update(p.encode("utf-8"))
+        h.update(b"\n")
+    return h.hexdigest()[:16]
+
+
+_SEG_ATOMS = [
+    "src",
+    "lib",
+    "test",
+    "tests",
+    "docs",
+    "build",
+    "dist",
+    "bin",
+    "obj",
+    "tmp",
+    "cache",
+    "node_modules",
+    "vendor",
+    "assets",
+    "data",
+    "out",
+]
+
+_FILE_ATOMS = [
+    "main.py",
+    "app.js",
+    "index.html",
+    "README.md",
+    "notes.txt",
+    "a.out",
+    "report.log",
+    "image.png",
+    "model.bin",
+    "archive.tar",
+    "archive.tar.gz",
+    ".env",
+]
+
+
+def _rand_segment(rng: random.Random) -> str:
+    base = rng.choice(_SEG_ATOMS)
+    if rng.random() < 0.15:
+        base = f"{base}{rng.randint(0, 9)}"
+    if rng.random() < 0.05:
+        base = base.replace("_", "-")
+    return base
+
+
+def _rand_path(rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[str, bool]:
+    depth = rng.randint(1, 4)
+    segs = [_rand_segment(rng) for _ in range(depth - 1)]
+    if rng.random() < 0.30:
+        # Directory path query.
+        segs.append(_rand_segment(rng))
+        return ("/".join(segs) + "/", True)
+    leaf = rng.choice(_FILE_ATOMS)
+    segs.append(leaf)
+    return ("/".join(segs), False)
+
+
+def _pattern_from_path(rng: random.Random, path: str) -> str:
+    # Produce a pattern likely to match the path, with controlled complexity.
+    s = path.rstrip("/")
+    segs = s.split("/")
+    choice = rng.random()
+    if choice < 0.30:
+        # Basename pattern
+        leaf = segs[-1]
+        if rng.random() < 0.35 and "." in leaf:
+            ext = leaf.split(".")[-1]
+            return f"*.{ext}"
+        if rng.random() < 0.20:
+            return leaf[0] + "?" + leaf[2:] if len(leaf) >= 3 else leaf
+        return leaf
+    if choice < 0.65:
+        # Directory pattern
+        d = segs[rng.randint(0, max(0, len(segs) - 2))]
+        return f"{d}/"
+    # Slash-containing pattern
+    prefix_len = rng.randint(1, min(len(segs), 3))
+    prefix = "/".join(segs[:prefix_len])
+    if rng.random() < 0.25:
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/**"
+    if rng.random() < 0.25 and prefix.endswith("**"):
+        prefix = f"{prefix}/*.log"
+    return prefix
+
+
+def _maybe_escape_prefix(rng: random.Random, pat: str) -> str:
+    if pat and pat[0] in ("#", "!") and rng.random() < 0.7:
+        return "\\" + pat
+    return pat
+
+
+def _make_gitignore(rng: random.Random, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    lines: List[str] = []
+    # Add some comments and blank lines
+    if rng.random() < 0.6:
+        lines.append("# IgnoreSense generated gitignore")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        lines.append("")
+
+    # Choose a few patterns derived from paths, plus some distractors.
+    chosen = rng.sample(paths, k=min(len(paths), rng.randint(4, 7)))
+    patterns: List[str] = []
+    for p, _is_dir in chosen:
+        patterns.append(_pattern_from_path(rng, p))
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.tmp")
+    if rng.random() < 0.5:
+        patterns.append("*.log")
+    if rng.random() < 0.3:
+        patterns.append("**/cache/**")
+
+    rng.shuffle(patterns)
+
+    # Add negations to create precedence traps.
+    negations: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns[:]:
+        if rng.random() < 0.25 and not pat.startswith("!"):
+            # Create a negation that partially overlaps
+            if pat.endswith("/"):
+                base = pat[:-1]
+                neg = f"!{base}/keep.*"
+            elif pat.startswith("*."):
+                neg = f"!important{pat[1:]}"
+            else:
+                neg = f"!{pat}"
+            negations.append(neg)
+
+    # Build final lines with occasional anchoring.
+    all_lines: List[str] = []
+    for pat in patterns + negations:
+        p = pat
+        if not p.startswith(("!", "\\")) and rng.random() < 0.2:
+            p = "/" + p
+        p = _maybe_escape_prefix(rng, p)
+        all_lines.append(p)
+
+    # Ensure at least one negation and one directory-only pattern in most items.
+    if not any(l.startswith("!") for l in all_lines):
+        all_lines.append("!README.md")
+    if not any(l.rstrip("\n").rstrip("\r").endswith("/") for l in all_lines if not l.startswith("#")):
+        all_lines.append("build/")
+
+    # Intermix some spacing and comment quirks
+    out: List[str] = []
+    for l in all_lines:
+        if rng.random() < 0.15:
+            out.append("  " + l)
+        else:
+            out.append(l)
+        if rng.random() < 0.10:
+            out.append("# trailing comment line")
+    return "\n".join(out) + "\n"
+
+
+def _compute_answer(gitignore_text: str, paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]]) -> str:
+    ignored: List[str] = []
+    for p, is_dir in paths:
+        if is_ignored(gitignore_text, p.rstrip("/"), is_dir=is_dir):
+            ignored.append(p)
+    ignored_sorted = sorted(ignored)
+    return json.dumps(ignored_sorted, ensure_ascii=False, separators=(",", ":"))
+
+
+def _write_jsonl(path: Path, rows: Iterable[dict]) -> None:
+    with path.open("w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
+        for row in rows:
+            f.write(json.dumps(row, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n")
+
+
+def main() -> None:
+    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser()
+    ap.add_argument("--sample-count", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--seed", type=int, required=True)
+    ap.add_argument("--out-dir", type=str, required=True)
+    args = ap.parse_args()
+
+    out_dir = Path(args.out_dir)
+    out_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+    solver_dir = out_dir / "solver_bundle"
+    solver_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
+
+    rng = random.Random(args.seed)
+
+    items_rows: List[dict] = []
+    gold_rows: List[dict] = []
+
+    for idx in range(args.sample_count):
+        # Create candidate paths with some duplicates removed.
+        raw_paths: List[Tuple[str, bool]] = []
+        while len(raw_paths) < 12:
+            p, is_dir = _rand_path(rng)
+            if (p, is_dir) not in raw_paths:
+                raw_paths.append((p, is_dir))
+
+        gitignore_text = _make_gitignore(rng, raw_paths)
+        paths_only = [p for p, _ in raw_paths]
+        item_id = _stable_id(args.seed, idx, gitignore_text, paths_only)
+
+        answer = _compute_answer(gitignore_text, raw_paths)
+        items_rows.append(
+            {
+                "id": item_id,
+                "gitignore": gitignore_text,
+                "paths": paths_only,
+            }
+        )
+        gold_rows.append({"id": item_id, "answer": answer})
+
+    _write_jsonl(solver_dir / "items_private_sample.jsonl", items_rows)
+    _write_jsonl(out_dir / "gold_private_sample.jsonl", gold_rows)
+
+    manifest = {
+        "benchmark_name": "IgnoreSense",
+        "benchmark_version": "1.0.0",
+        "items_file": "items_private_sample.jsonl",
+        "answer_format": "JSON array of ignored paths sorted lexicographically; answer is serialized as a compact JSON string.",
+        "notes": [
+            "All tasks are self-contained; do not assume full gitignore semantics beyond what the packet describes.",
+            "Paths use '/' separators and are relative (no leading './'). Directory paths end with '/'.",
+        ],
+    }
+    (solver_dir / "SOLVER_MANIFEST.json").write_text(
+        json.dumps(manifest, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + "\n", encoding="utf-8"
+    )
+
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    main()
+
